This bit can change only\\n73: \\t// (1) during a call to StartRequest and (2) during a call to\\n74: \\t// Request::Finish.  In the latter case idleness can only change\\n75: \\t// from false to true.\\n76: \\tIsIdle() bool\\n77: \\n78: \\t// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request. The\\n82: \\t// descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but appear\\n83: \\t// in log messages.  This method always returns quickly (without\\n84: \\t// waiting for the request to be dequeued). They\n30: // are separated so that errors from the first phase can be found\n31: // before committing to a concurrency allotment for the second.\n32: type QueueSetFactory interface {\n33: \t// BeginConstruction does the first phase of creating a QueueSet.\n34: \t// The RatioedGaugePair observes number of requests,\n35: \t// execution covering just the regular phase.\n36: \t// The denominator for the waiting phase is\n37: \t// max(1, QueuingConfig.QueueLengthLimit) X max(1, QueuingConfig.DesiredNumQueues).\n38: \t// The RatioedGauge observes number of seats occupied through all phases of execution.\n39: \t// The denominator for all the ratioed concurrency gauges is supplied later in the DispatchingConfig.\n40: \t// The Gauge observes the seat demand (executing + queued seats).\n41: \tBeginConstruction(QueuingConfig, metrics.RatioedGaugePair, metrics.RatioedGauge, metrics.Gauge) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n42: }\n43: \n44: // QueueSetCompleter finishes the two-step process of creating or\n45: // reconfiguring a QueueSet\n46: type QueueSetCompleter interface {\n47: \t// Complete returns a QueueSet configured by the given\n48: \t// dispatching configuration.\n49: \tComplete(DispatchingConfig) QueueSet\n50: }\n51: \n52: // QueueSet is the abstraction for the queuing and dispatching\n53: // functionality of one non-exempt priority level.  It covers the\n54: // functionality described in the \"Assignment to a Queue\", \"Queuing\",\n55: // and \"Dispatching\" sections of\n56: // https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\n57: // .  Some day we may have connections between priority levels, but\n58: // today is not that day.\n59: type QueueSet interface {\n60: \t// BeginConfigChange starts the two-step process of updating the\n61: \t// configuration.  No change is made until Complete is called.  If\n62: \t// `C := X.BeginConstruction(q)` then `C.Complete(d)` returns the\n63: \t// same value `X`.  If the QueuingConfig's DesiredNumQueues field\n64: \t// is zero then the other queuing-specific config parameters are\n65: \t// not changed, so that the queues continue draining as before.\n66: \t// In any case, reconfiguration does not discard any queue unless\n67: \t// and until it is undesired and empty.\n68: \tBeginConfigChange(QueuingConfig) (QueueSetCompleter, error)\n69: \n70: \t// IsIdle returns a bool indicating whether the QueueSet was idle\n71: \t// at the moment of the return.  Idle means the QueueSet has zero\n72: \t// requests queued and zero executing.  This bit can change only\n73: \t// (1) during a call to StartRequest and (2) during a call to\n74: \t// Request::Finish.  In the latter case idleness can only change\n75: \t// from false to true.\n76: \tIsIdle() bool\n77: \n78: \t// StartRequest begins the process of handling a request.  If the\n79: \t// request gets queued and the number of queues is greater than 1\n80: \t// then StartRequest uses the given hashValue as the source of\n81: \t// entropy as it shuffle-shards the request into a queue.  The\n82: \t// descr1 and descr2 values play no role in the logic but appear\n83: \t// in log messages.  This method always returns quickly (without\n84: \t// waiting for the request to be dequeued). Otherwise idle==false\n88: \t// and the client must call the Finish method of the Request\n89: \t// exactly once.\n90: \tStartRequest(ctx context.Context, width *request.WorkEstimate, hashValue uint64, flowDistinguisher, fsName string, descr1, descr2 interface{}, queueNoteFn QueueNoteFn) (req Request, idle bool)\n91: \n92: \t// Dump saves and returns the instant internal state of the queue-set.\n93: \t// Note that dumping process will stop the queue-set from proceeding\n94: \t// any requests.\n95: \t// For debugging only.\n96: \tDump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump\n97: }\n98: \n99: // QueueNoteFn is called when a request enters and leaves a queue\n100: type QueueNoteFn func(inQueue bool)\n101: \n102: // Request represents the remainder of the handling of one request\n103: type Request interface {\n104: \t// Finish determines whether to execute or reject the request and\n105: \t// invokes `execute` if the decision is to execute the request.\n106: \t// The returned `idle bool` value indicates whether the QueueSet\n107: \t// was idle when the value was calculated, but might no longer be\n108: \t// accurate by the time the client examines that value.\n109: \tFinish(execute func()) (idle bool)\n110: }\n111: \n112: // QueuingConfig defines the configuration of the queuing aspect of a QueueSet.\n113: type QueuingConfig struct {\n114: \t// Name is used to identify a queue set, allowing for descriptive information about its intended use\n115: \tName string\n116: \n117: \t// DesiredNumQueues is the number of queues that the API says\n118: \t// should exist now.  This may be non-positive, in which case\n119: \t// QueueLengthLimit, and HandSize are ignored.\n120: \t// A value of zero means to respect the ConcurrencyLimit of the DispatchingConfig.\n121: \t// A negative value means to always dispatch immediately upon arrival\n122: \t// (i.e., the requests are \"exempt\" from limitation).\n123: \tDesiredNumQueues int\n124: \n125: \t// QueueLengthLimit is the maximum number of requests that may be waiting in a given queue at a time\n126: \tQueueLengthLimit int\n127: \n128: \t// HandSize is a parameter of shuffle sharding.  Upon arrival of a request, a queue is chosen by randomly\n129: \t// dealing a \"hand\" of this many queues and then picking one of minimum length.\n130: \tHandSize int\n131: }\n132: \n133: // DispatchingConfig defines the configuration of the dispatching aspect of a QueueSet.\n134: type DispatchingConfig struct {\n135: \t// ConcurrencyLimit is the maximum number of requests of this QueueSet that may be executing at a time\n136: \tConcurrencyLimit int\n137: \n138: \t// ConcurrencyDenominator is used in relative metrics of concurrency.\n139: \t// It equals ConcurrencyLimit except when that is zero.\n140: \tConcurrencyDenominator int\n141: }\n142: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go"}}}

One QueueSet is a set of queues operating\\n19: // according to this technique.\\n20: //\\n21: // Fair queuing for server requests is inspired by the fair queuing\\n22: // technique from the world of networking.  You can find a good paper\\n23: // on that at https://dl.acm.org/citation.cfm?doid=75247.75248 or\\n24: // http://people.csail.mit.edu/imcgraw/links/research/pubs/networks/WFQ.pdf\\n25: // and there is an implementation outline in the Wikipedia article at\\n26: // https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fair_queuing .\\n27: //\\n28: // Fair queuing for server requests differs from traditional fair\\n29: // queuing in three ways: (1) we are dispatching application layer\\n30: // requests to a server rather than transmitting packets on a network\\n31: // link, (2) multiple requests can be executing at once, and (3) the\\n32: // service time (execution duration) is not known until the execution\\n33: // completes.\\n34: //\\n35: // The first two differences can easily be handled by straightforward\\n36: // adaptation of the concept called \\\"R(t)\\\" in the original paper and\\n37: // \\\"virtual time\\\" in the implementation outline. In that\\n38: // implementation outline, the notation now() is used to mean reading\\n39: // the virtual clock. In the original paper’s terms, \\\"R(t)\\\" is the\\n40: // number of \\\"rounds\\\" that have been completed at real time t ---\\n41: // where a round consists of virtually transmitting one bit from every\\n42: // non-empty queue in the router (regardless of which queue holds the\\n43: // packet that is really being transmitted at the moment); in this\\n44: // conception, a packet is considered to be \\\"in\\\" its queue until the\\n45: // packet’s transmission is finished. For our problem, we can define a\\n46: // round to be giving one nanosecond of CPU to every non-empty queue\\n47: // in the apiserver (where emptiness is judged based on both queued\\n48: // and executing requests from that queue), and define R(t) = (server\\n49: // start time) + (1 ns) * (number of rounds since server start). Let\\n50: // us write NEQ(t) for that number of non-empty queues in the\\n51: // apiserver at time t.  Let us also write C for the concurrency\\n52: // limit.  In the original paper, the partial derivative of R(t) with\\n53: // respect to t is\\n54: //\\n55: //\\t1 / NEQ(t) .\\n56: //\\n57: // To generalize from transmitting one packet at a time to executing C\\n58: // requests at a time, that derivative becomes\\n59: //\\n60: //\\tC / NEQ(t) .\\n61: //\\n62: // However, sometimes there are fewer than C requests available to\\n63: // execute.  For a given queue \\\"q\\\", let us also write \\\"reqs(q, t)\\\" for\\n64: // the number of requests of that queue that are executing at that\\n65: // time.  The total number of requests executing is sum[over q]\\n66: // reqs(q, t) and if that is less than C then virtual time is not\\n67: // advancing as fast as it would if all C seats were occupied; in this\\n68: // case the numerator of the quotient in that derivative should be\\n69: // adjusted proportionally.  Putting it all together for fair queing\\n70: // for server requests: at a particular time t, the partial derivative\\n71: // of R(t) with respect to t is\\n72: //\\n73: //\\tmin( C, sum[over q] reqs(q, t) ) / NEQ(t) .\\n74: //\\n75: // In terms of the implementation outline, this is the rate at which\\n76: // virtual time is advancing at time t (in virtual nanoseconds per\\n77: // real nanosecond). Where the networking implementation outline adds\\n78: // packet size to a virtual time, in our version this corresponds to\\n79: // adding a service time (i.e., duration) to virtual time.\\n80: //\\n81: // The third difference is handled by modifying the algorithm to\\n82: // dispatch based on an initial guess at the request’s service time\\n83: // (duration) and then make the corresponding adjustments once the\\n84: // request’s actual service time is known. In plain fair queuing the bound is one packet; in our\\n97: // version it is C requests.\\n98: //\\n99: // To support efficiently making the necessary adjustments once a\\n100: // request’s actual service time is known, the virtual finish time of\\n101: // a request and the last virtual finish time of a queue are not\\n102: // represented directly but instead computed from queue length,\\n103: // request position in the queue, and an alternate state variable that\\n104: // holds the queue’s virtual start time. While the queue is empty and\\n105: // has no requests executing: the value of its virtual start time\\n106: // variable is ignored and its last virtual finish time is considered\\n107: // to be in the virtual past. When a request arrives to an empty queue\\n108: // with no requests executing, the queue’s virtual start time is set\\n109: // to the current virtual time. The fields listed before the lock\\n71: // should not be changed; the fields listed after the\\n72: // lock must be accessed only while holding the lock.\\n73: //\\n74: // The methods of this type follow the naming convention that the\\n75: // suffix \\\"Locked\\\" means the caller must hold the lock; for a method\\n76: // whose name does not end in \\\"Locked\\\" either acquires the lock or\\n77: // does not care about locking.\\n78: //\\n79: // The methods of this type also follow the convention that the suffix\\n80: // \\\"ToBoundLocked\\\" means that the caller may have to follow up with a\\n81: // call to `boundNextDispatchLocked`.  This is so for a method that\\n82: // changes what request is oldest in a queue, because that change means\\n83: // that the anti-windup hack in boundNextDispatchLocked needs to be\\n84: // applied wrt the revised oldest request in the queue.\\n85: type queueSet struct {\\n86: \\tclock                    eventclock.Interface\\n87: \\testimatedServiceDuration time.Duration\\n88: \\n89: \\treqsGaugePair metrics.RatioedGaugePair // .RequestsExecuting covers regular phase only\\n90: \\n91: \\texecSeatsGauge metrics.RatioedGauge // for all phases of execution\\n92: \\n93: \\tseatDemandIntegrator metrics.Gauge\\n94: \\n95: \\tpromiseFactory promiseFactory\\n96: \\n97: \\tlock sync.Mutex\\n98: \\n99: \\t// qCfg holds the current queuing configuration. i < len(keptQueues); i++ {\n991: \t\tkeptQueues[i].index--\n992: \t}\n993: \treturn keptQueues\n994: }\n995: \n996: func (qs *queueSet) Dump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump {\n997: \tqs.lock.Lock()\n998: \tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n999: \td := debug.QueueSetDump{\n1000: \t\tQueues:                     make([]debug.QueueDump, len(qs.queues)),\n1001: \t\tQueuelessExecutingRequests: SetMapReduce(dumpRequest(includeRequestDetails), append1[debug.RequestDump])(qs.requestsExecutingSet),\n1002: \t\tWaiting:                    qs.totRequestsWaiting,\n1003: \t\tExecuting:                  qs.totRequestsExecuting,\n1004: \t\tSeatsInUse:                 qs.totSeatsInUse,\n1005: \t\tSeatsWaiting:               qs.totSeatsWaiting,\n1006: \t\tDispatched:                 qs.totRequestsDispatched,\n1007: \t\tRejected:                   qs.totRequestsRejected,\n1008: \t\tTimedout:                   qs.totRequestsTimedout,\n1009: \t\tCancelled:                  qs.totRequestsCancelled,\n1010: \t}\n1011: \tfor i, q := range qs.queues {\n1012: \t\td.Queues[i] = q.dumpLocked(includeRequestDetails)\n1013: \t}\n1014: \treturn d\n1015: }\n1016: \n1017: func OnRequestDispatched(r fq.Request) {\n1018: \treq, ok := r.(*request)\n1019: \tif !ok {\n1020: \t\treturn\n1021: \t}\n1022: \n1023: \tqs := req.qs\n1024: \tif qs != nil {\n1025: \t\tqs.lock.Lock()\n1026: \t\tdefer qs.lock.Unlock()\n1027: \t\tqs.totRequestsDispatched++\n1028: \t}\n1029: }\n1030: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kubernetes--8c9c67c0@8c9c67c000104450cfc5a5f48053a9a84b73cf93/-/blob/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go"}}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01JMf7a3urT1mnuyam4P3bar","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01UcYjVXQcDKpwresZcE8SFf","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe Advanced Priority and Fairness (APF) QueueSet is Kubernetes's implementation of Fair Queuing for Server Requests—an algorithm adapted from network packet scheduling. It enforces prioritization and fairness across API server requests by using virtual time tracking, multi-queue load balancing via shuffle sharding, and dynamic concurrency control. This document explains the design, flow, and operational tradeoffs that shape the system's behavior.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe APF QueueSet subsystem implements fair queuing to:\n- **Enforce priority levels** across authenticated and privileged requests via separate QueueSets per priority level\n- **Distribute requests fairly** within a priority level using shuffle-sharded queues\n- **Prevent starvation** by using virtual time to bound per-flow divergence from ideal fair allocation\n- **Support multi-seated requests** where a request occupies multiple \"seats\" (concurrency slots), accounting for variable request widths\n- **Enable borrowing** by tracking seat demand and allowing dynamic reallocation among priority levels\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**Upstream dependencies:**\n- APF Controller (`apf_controller.go`) provisions QueueSets per priority level, manages configurations\n- Flow Schema matching determines request classification and hash value for shuffle sharding\n- Request rate limiting filter (`apf_filter.go`) invokes StartRequest/Finish lifecycle\n\n**Downstream dependencies:**\n- Metrics system observes queue depths, waiting/executing request counts, seat concurrency, and epoch advances\n- EventClock interface provides real and virtual time for progress meter advancement\n- Promise mechanism (WriteOnce) coordinates dispatch decision communication between dispatch loop and request waiter\n\n**Not in scope:**\n- Flow Schema evaluation or request matching (upstream responsibility)\n- Exempt request handling (separate fast path, no queuing)\n- Per-request authentication or authorization validation\n\n### Key Architectural Constraints\n\n1. **Lock discipline:** All mutable queue state is protected by a single queueSet-level mutex. Virtual time updates (syncTimeLocked) must precede state mutations.\n2. **Promise-based dispatch:** Dispatch decisions are communicated via a WriteOnce promise set under lock; request threads wait without lock to avoid deadlock.\n3. **No cross-priority-level coordination:** Each QueueSet operates independently; borrowing is managed at the controller level by adjusting ConcurrencyLimits.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### QueueSet (`queueset.go`, `types.go`)\n\nThe core fair-queuing engine. Fields (under lock):\n\n| Field | Responsibility |\n|-------|---|\n| `queues []*queue` | Ordered array of fair-share queues, index tracked per request arrival |\n| `currentR SeatSeconds` | Global virtual time (progress meter), advanced by syncTimeLocked |\n| `dealer *Dealer` | Shuffle sharding parameters; picks a queue via entropy from request hash |\n| `totSeatsInUse`, `totSeatsWaiting` | Tracks seat occupancy for concurrency enforcement |\n| `totRequestsWaiting`, `totRequestsExecuting` | Metrics for queue depth and execution |\n\n**Key invariants:**\n- Virtual time only moves forward; epoch advancement prevents overflow (lines 489-522)\n- Every request in a queue has `arrivalR ≤ queue.nextDispatchR` (anti-windup bound, line 952-963)\n- Seats in use never exceed `dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit` except during grace periods for large single requests\n\n### Queue (`types.go`)\n\nRepresents a fair-share queue within a QueueSet. Fields:\n\n| Field | Responsibility |\n|-------|---|\n| `requestsWaiting fifo` | FIFO list of requests awaiting dispatch |\n| `requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]` | Requests currently executing from this queue |\n| `nextDispatchR SeatSeconds` | Virtual start time of the queue's allocated window |\n| `seatsInUse int` | Total seats held by executing requests from this queue |\n\n**Why per-queue tracking?** Allows virtual time calculation to reflect per-flow fairness.\n\n### Request (`types.go`)\n\nTracks a request's state through the system. Lifecycle:\n\n1. Created in `shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked` with `arrivalR = currentR`\n2. Enqueued into selected queue's `requestsWaiting` FIFO\n3. Dequeued in `dispatchLocked`, moved to queue's `requestsExecuting`, decision set to `decisionExecute`\n4. Request thread calls `Finish(execute)`, which calls `finishRequestLocked`\n5. Seats may linger if `AdditionalLatency > 0` (multi-phase request completion)\n\n**Work estimate tracking:**\n- `InitialSeats`: seats for primary execution phase\n- `FinalSeats` + `AdditionalLatency`: seats held post-completion (L7 processing, response marshaling)\n- Actual service duration adjusts queue's virtual start via `queue.nextDispatchR -= (G - S) * width`\n\n### FIFO List (`fifo_list.go`)\n\nA doubly-linked list with O(1) removal via closure. Tracks aggregate `queueSum` (InitialSeatsSum, MaxSeatsSum, TotalWorkSum) to avoid O(n) scans when selecting queues during shuffle sharding.\n\n### Shuffle Sharding Dealer (`shufflesharding.go`)\n\nImplements a card-dealing algorithm (entropy consumption: `log₂(deckSize) × handSize` bits). Given a hash value:\n\n1. Randomly select `handSize` queue indices from `deckSize` total queues\n2. Among selected hand, pick the queue with the **minimum total work** in waiting requests\n3. Reuse the same hand across multiple arrivals to reduce variance\n\n**Why shuffle sharding?** Prevents hash collisions from concentrating misbehaving flows into a single queue, improving isolation.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow with Concrete Evidence\n\n### Phase 1: Request Arrival (StartRequest)\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:308-356`\n\n```\nStartRequest(ctx, workEstimate, hashValue, fsName, ...)\n  ↓ lockAndSyncTime(ctx)  // acquire lock; sync virtual time\n  ↓ syncTimeLocked(ctx)   // advance currentR based on elapsed real time\n     • incrR = (min(totSeatsInUse, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues) * timeSinceLast\n     • if currentR ≥ highR, call advanceEpoch to prevent overflow\n  ↓ Case 1: DesiredNumQueues < 1 (exempt fast path)\n     • canAccommodateSeatsLocked checks if max seat requirement ≤ available\n     • dispatchSansQueueLocked creates request, immediately sets decision=decisionExecute\n     • return (req, false)\n  ↓ Case 2: DesiredNumQueues ≥ 1 (queued path)\n     • shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked(workEstimate, hashValue, ...)\n       ├─ shuffleShardLocked: dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue)\n       │  ├─ random permutation via entropy bits\n       │  └─ pick queue with min(queueSum.TotalWorkSum)\n       ├─ rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked\n       │  ├─ reject if totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit AND curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit\n       │  └─ else enqueueToBoundLocked:\n       │     ├─ if queue was empty, set queue.nextDispatchR = currentR\n       │     ├─ enqueue to queue.requestsWaiting FIFO\n       │     ├─ update metrics (requests waiting, seats waiting, queue length)\n       │     └─ return request\n       └─ return req or nil (if rejected)\n  ↓ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked\n     • loop: while totRequestsWaiting > 0 AND totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit\n       ├─ findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked: round-robin through queues\n       │  ├─ scan for queue with min(queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork())\n       │  ├─ check canAccommodateSeatsLocked\n       │  └─ if cannot accommodate, set AdditionalLatency to preserve work\n       └─ dispatchLocked: dequeue from winning queue, set decision=decisionExecute\n  ↓ unlock\n  ↓ return (req, isIdleLocked)\n```\n\n**Key metric updates at arrival:** `RequestsWaiting.Add(1)`, `SeatsWaiting += maxSeats`, `SeatDemandIntegrator.Set(...)`\n\n### Phase 2: Request Dispatch\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:695-743`\n\nThe dispatch loop runs **synchronously** inside StartRequest. Virtual time must be consistent during dispatch because multiple requests may be dispatched in the same call.\n\n```\ndispatchLocked() → findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()\n  ↓ Round-robin through queues (starting after last dispatched queue)\n  ↓ For each non-empty queue:\n     • peekOldest from requestsWaiting\n     • compute currentVirtualFinish = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()\n     • track min(currentVirtualFinish)\n  ↓ Check if winning queue's head can accommodate seats\n     • if canAccommodateSeatsLocked fails:\n       ├─ wait for executing requests to complete\n       ├─ return (nil, nil) → no dispatch\n       └─ metrics.AddDispatchWithNoAccommodation\n  ↓ Handle multi-seated final phase\n     • if FinalSeats > ConcurrencyLimit:\n       ├─ reduce FinalSeats to ConcurrencyLimit\n       ├─ adjust AdditionalLatency to preserve total work\n  ↓ Set robinIndex for next round\n  ↓ Decision: set decision.Set(decisionExecute)\n     • if promise already resolved (request cancelled), don't move to executing\n  ↓ Move to queue.requestsExecuting\n  ↓ Advance queue's virtual start:\n     queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n  ↓ Return (queue, request)\n```\n\n**Anti-windup hack (boundNextDispatchLocked, line 952-963):**\nPrevent a low-demand queue from accumulating a negative virtual start:\n```go\nif queue.nextDispatchR < oldestWaiting.arrivalR {\n    queue.nextDispatchR = oldestWaiting.arrivalR\n}\n```\nThis ensures dispatch never precedes arrival in the virtual world.\n\n### Phase 3: Request Execution & Completion (Finish)\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:381-441` (request wrapper), `queueset.go:863-943` (finishRequestLocked)\n\n```\nreq.Finish(execFn)\n  ↓ req.wait()  // without lock\n     • decisionAny := req.decision.Get()  // blocks until dispatch decision made\n     • lockAndSyncTime(req.ctx)\n     • if decisionAny == decisionCancel (context expired before dispatch):\n       ├─ remove from queue\n       ├─ update metrics (requests rejected, timeout)\n       └─ return (false, isIdleLocked)\n     • else decisionExecute:\n       └─ return (true, false)\n  ↓ if execute:\n     • defer finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(req)\n     • execFn()  // run user code\n  ↓ finishRequestLocked(req)\n     • actualServiceDuration := now - req.startTime\n     • adjust queue.nextDispatchR by (G - actualServiceDuration) * width\n     • update totSeatsInUse -= maxSeats\n     • if AdditionalLatency > 0:\n       ├─ schedule delayed seat release via EventAfterDuration\n       └─ metrics for lingering seats\n     • remove from queue.requestsExecuting\n     • try removeQueueIfEmptyLocked if queue exceeds desired count\n  ↓ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()  // cascade dispatch\n  ↓ return isIdleLocked\n```\n\n**Why two-phase seat release?**\nInitialSeats are released when actual work completes. FinalSeats (e.g., response marshaling) are held for AdditionalLatency to avoid blocking the next request. This improves pipelining.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Virtual Time & Fairness Algorithm\n\n### Virtual Time Advancement (syncTimeLocked)\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:465-479`\n\n```\nsyncTimeLocked(ctx):\n  realNow := clock.Now()\n  timeSinceLast := realNow - lastRealTime\n  lastRealTime = realNow\n\n  ratio := getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()\n    // = min(seatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n    // where seatsRequested = sum over queues of (seatsInUse + queueSum.MaxSeatsSum)\n\n  incrR := SeatsTimesDuration(ratio, timeSinceLast)\n  currentR += incrR\n\n  if currentR ≥ highR:\n    advanceEpoch()  // subtract rDecrement from all R values to prevent overflow\n```\n\n**Intuition:** Virtual time advances at a rate proportional to:\n- How much concurrency is in use vs. available (fairness to other flows)\n- How many non-empty queues are competing (fair share per queue)\n\n### Virtual Finish Time Calculation\n\nWhen a request is dequeued at time T with work estimate W:\n```\nvirtualFinishTime = queue.nextDispatchR + W\n```\n\nThe dispatch loop picks the queue with the **minimum virtual finish time**, ensuring FIFO within each queue but round-robin fairness across queues.\n\n### Work Estimate Adjustment\n\nAt finish, if actual service time S < estimated G:\n```\nqueue.nextDispatchR -= (G - S) * width\n```\n\nThis **penalizes** queues that underutilized their allocated time, preventing them from gaining unfair advantage from optimistic estimates.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### Failure Mode: Overflow Prevention\n\n**Risk:** Virtual time counter can overflow (64-bit signed SeatSeconds).\n\n**Mitigation (advanceEpoch, line 489-522):**\n- When `currentR ≥ highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2`, subtract `rDecrement = MaxSeatSeconds/2` from all R values\n- Applied to: `currentR`, all `queue.nextDispatchR`, all `request.arrivalR`\n- Logged as `AddEpochAdvance` metric\n\n**Tradeoff:** Periodic correction adds complexity but avoids unbounded R growth over months of operation.\n\n### Failure Mode: Concurrent Wide Requests\n\n**Risk:** A single request with `MaxSeats > ConcurrencyLimit` can fail to dispatch.\n\n**Mitigation (canAccommodateSeatsLocked, line 748-769):**\n```go\nif seats > qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit:\n    if qs.totRequestsExecuting == 0:\n        return true  // Allow it to run alone\n    else:\n        return false  // Wait for others to finish\n```\nThis enforces **exclusive execution** for requests wider than the concurrency limit.\n\n**Tradeoff:** May block other requests unfairly, but prevents deadlock. Mitigated by work estimator bounds (typically max 15% of limit).\n\n### Failure Mode: Queue Starvation During Reconfiguration\n\n**Risk:** If `DesiredNumQueues` is reduced, empty queues are removed by attrition. A queue with stuck requests might linger.\n\n**Mitigation (removeQueueIfEmptyLocked, line 966-984):**\n- Only remove queue if:\n  - `len(queues) > DesiredNumQueues` AND\n  - `queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0` AND\n  - `queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0`\n- Update `robinIndex` if removed queue was at or before current position\n\n**Tradeoff:** Manual draining required; admins must monitor `queue.requestsWaiting.Length()` to ensure cleanup.\n\n### Design Tradeoff: Shuffle Sharding Parameters\n\n| Setting | Effect | Tradeoff |\n|---------|--------|----------|\n| `queues=1` | No shuffle sharding; all flows share one queue | Simple, fair allocation; misbehaving flow starves others |\n| `queues=128, handSize=4` | Each flow hashed to one of C(128,4) hands | Good isolation; higher entropy cost, memory overhead |\n| `handSize=handSize` near `queues` | More selective queue picking | Isolation but higher lock contention if many flows |\n\n**Guidance:** handSize typically 4–8; queues scaled to expected flow count.\n\n### Design Tradeoff: Estimated Service Duration (G)\n\n**Current:** Fixed at 3ms per QueueSet (line 215 in queueset.go).\n\n**Effect:**\n- Used to estimate initial work: `InitialWork = InitialSeats * G`\n- Used to penalize underutilization: `queue.nextDispatchR -= (G - actual) * width`\n\n**Tradeoff:**\n- Too high: Queues underutilize allocated time, starving other queues\n- Too low: Overestimate work, inflate queue's virtual finish time, allow preemption\n- Fixed value assumes uniform request characteristics; not tunable per priority level\n\n**Mitigation:** Request.AdditionalLatency allows explicit work accounting post-completion.\n\n### Design Tradeoff: Single Global Lock\n\nAll mutable queue state is protected by `queueSet.lock`.\n\n**Benefit:** Simple correctness reasoning; atomic state updates.\n\n**Cost:**\n- Lock contention under high request rate\n- StartRequest must synchronously dispatch requests (cannot pipeline)\n- Mitigation: `syncTimeLocked` deferred until next lock acquisition to reduce critical section\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### Promise Factory (testability)\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:47-54`\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactory func(initial, doneCtx, doneVal) promise.WriteOnce\ntype promiseFactoryFactory func(*queueSet) promiseFactory\n```\n\nDefault: `ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory` returns `promise.NewWriteOnce`.\n\n**Extension:** Test code can provide a different factory to control promise resolution timing, simulate slow dispatch, or verify dispatch order.\n\n**Risk:** Incorrect factory can cause deadlocks or race conditions; not recommended for production use.\n\n### Clock Interface\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:86`, `fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go`\n\nQueueSet uses an `eventclock.Interface` for:\n- `Now()`: current time for virtual time advancement\n- `EventAfterDuration(func, duration)`: schedule delayed seat release\n\n**Extension:** Custom clocks (e.g., simulation time) allow deterministic testing.\n\n**Risk:** Clock skew or backwards time can cause virtual time inversion or epoch advances to fail validation (line 507-509).\n\n### Metrics Integration\n\n**Code reference:** `metrics/metrics.go`\n\nQueueSet reports to:\n- `RatioedGaugePair.RequestsWaiting/Executing`: per-queue, per-flow-schema\n- `RatioedGauge.ExecSeatsGauge`: per-priority-level\n- `Gauge.SeatDemandIntegrator`: integral of (executing + waiting seats) over time\n\n**Extension:** Controller uses integrator output to drive borrowing adjustments (seat demand stats smoothing).\n\n**Risk:** Incorrect metrics can mask actual queue state; useful for observability but not for control decisions.\n\n### Dump for Debugging\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:996-1015`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) Dump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump\n```\n\nReturns instant snapshot of all queues, requests, and metrics (including user info if requested). Used by debug endpoints.\n\n**Extension:** Can be called from outside lock to expose internal state without blocking.\n\n**Risk:** Snapshot inconsistency under high load; suitable only for offline debugging, not runtime decision-making.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications & Failure Scenarios\n\n### Performance Implications\n\n#### Lock Contention\n\nUnder high request rates (e.g., 10k req/sec per QueueSet):\n- Each StartRequest acquires lock, syncs time, dispatches requests\n- Expected hold time: 100–500 μs per lock (dispatch loop iterations + FIFO ops)\n- If CPU-bound: lock contention can spike tail latencies\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Increase `DesiredNumQueues` to reduce per-queue depth (shallower FIFO searches)\n- Distribute flows across multiple priority levels if possible\n- Monitor `apiserver_flowcontrol_*_lock_*` metrics (if available)\n\n#### Virtual Time Skew Under Bursty Load\n\nIf execution is bursty (e.g., GC pause), virtual time may lag:\n```\nincrR = min(actualSeats, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues * timeSinceLast\n```\nDuring pause, `actualSeats` drops, so `incrR` ≈ 0. When requests resume, accumulated waiting requests have `arrivalR << currentR`, causing them to dispatch FIFO (fairness breaks temporarily).\n\n**Mitigation:** Virtual time is local to each priority level; system GC less likely to affect all levels equally.\n\n#### Epoch Advance Overhead\n\n`advanceEpoch` walks all queues and all waiting requests (O(Q + W) where Q = queue count, W = waiting requests). Under heavy queueing (100k+ waiting requests), this can stall dispatch for milliseconds.\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Tune `estimatedServiceDuration` to reduce work estimates (less queue depth)\n- Monitor `AddEpochAdvance` metric; if frequent, investigate cause (e.g., concurrency limit too low)\n\n### Reliability Implications\n\n#### Queue Draining on Priority Level Reconfiguration\n\nWhen a priority level is reconfigured (e.g., `DesiredNumQueues` decreased):\n1. New requests hash to remaining queues\n2. Old queues drain by attrition (removeQueueIfEmptyLocked)\n3. Until queue is empty, robinIndex remains valid\n\n**Risk:** Stuck requests prevent queue removal. Admins must monitor queue depth and manually investigate if queue doesn't drain within expected time.\n\n**Mitigation:** Set up alerts on `apiserver_flowcontrol_queues_length_*` metric; investigate requests with long `ArriveTime - StartTime`.\n\n#### Metrics Staleness During High Concurrency\n\n`SeatDemandIntegrator` tracks integral of seat usage. Under extreme concurrency:\n- Integrator value is only updated when:\n  - Request enqueued\n  - Request dequeued\n  - Request finishes\n- If no changes occur, integrator value lags real demand\n\n**Mitigation:** Integrator is smoothed (half-life ~5 min) before borrowing decisions; short-term fluctuations don't affect concurrency allocation.\n\n### Observability & Debugging\n\n**Key metrics to monitor:**\n\n| Metric | Interpretation |\n|--------|---|\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_queues_length_*` | Queue depth per priority level; increasing → admission too high or dispatch slow |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_seat_demand_*` | Integral of occupied seats; used for borrowing decisions |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advance_total` | How often virtual time is reset; high frequency → R values large, possible performance impact |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatch_with_no_accommodation` | Requests waiting for seats to free up; high → concurrency limit too low or request widths too high |\n\n**Debug endpoint** (`/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_queues`):\n- Provides per-queue snapshot with request details\n- Useful to correlate metrics with actual queue state\n- Can be called frequently without lock contention (outside queueset lock)\n\n---\n\n## 8. Important Files and Directory Map\n\n### Core QueueSet Implementation\n\n| Path | Responsibility |\n|------|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go` | QueueSet, Request, QueueSetFactory interfaces; QueuingConfig, DispatchingConfig |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go` | queueSet struct, StartRequest, dispatch loop, virtual time sync, epoch advance |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go` | request, queue, queueSum structs; work estimation helpers |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go` | FIFO list with O(1) removal; queue sum tracking |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/doc.go` | Fair queuing algorithm explanation; virtual time definitions |\n\n### Shuffle Sharding & Entropy\n\n| Path | Responsibility |\n|------|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go` | Dealer: shuffle sharding card dealing; entropy calculation |\n\n### APF Controller Integration\n\n| Path | Responsibility |\n|------|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go` | Configuration controller; Summary Table: Request Lifecycle State Transitions\n\n| State | Condition | Location | Next |\n|-------|-----------|----------|------|\n| Created | In `StartRequest`, hash computed | queueset.go:560 | → Rejected or Queued |\n| Rejected | `rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked` returns false | queueset.go:574 | END (return nil) |\n| Queued | Enqueued in `queue.requestsWaiting` | queueset.go:643 | → Dispatched or Cancelled |\n| Dispatched | `dispatchLocked` moves to `queue.requestsExecuting`, decision=decisionExecute | queueset.go:710–727 | → Executing |\n| Executing | Request handler runs `execFn` | queueset.go:391 | → Finished |\n| Cancelled | Context cancelled before dispatch, decision=decisionCancel | queueset.go:415 | END (return false) |\n| Finished | `finishRequestLocked` called, seats released or scheduled for release | queueset.go:863–943 | END (return idle) |\n\n---\n\n## 10. Conclusion\n\nThe APF QueueSet is a sophisticated fair-queuing implementation that balances **fairness** (virtual time), **isolation** (shuffle sharding), **concurrency control** (seat-based limiting), and **adaptability** (borrowing). Its success depends on:\n\n1. **Accurate work estimates** to tune virtual time advancement\n2. **Appropriate queue counts** to reduce per-queue depth and lock contention\n3. **Careful priority level configuration** to align with actual request patterns\n4. **Monitoring key metrics** (queue depth, seat demand, epoch advances) to detect imbalances\n\nOperational risks are primarily around **queue draining during reconfiguration**, **lock contention under extreme load**, and **overflow protection** via periodic epoch advances. Understanding these tradeoffs is essential for effective APF tuning and troubleshooting in production Kubernetes clusters.\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1941,"cache_read_input_tokens":82097,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1941},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"0e54a5f2-acb3-4fb7-be97-12a4d938314e","uuid":"832a7080-d928-4bac-91b8-cf7fa2601cfa"}

It enforces prioritization and fairness across API server requests by using virtual time tracking, multi-queue load balancing via shuffle sharding, and dynamic concurrency control. This document explains the design, flow, and operational tradeoffs that shape the system's behavior.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe APF QueueSet subsystem implements fair queuing to:\n- **Enforce priority levels** across authenticated and privileged requests via separate QueueSets per priority level\n- **Distribute requests fairly** within a priority level using shuffle-sharded queues\n- **Prevent starvation** by using virtual time to bound per-flow divergence from ideal fair allocation\n- **Support multi-seated requests** where a request occupies multiple \"seats\" (concurrency slots), accounting for variable request widths\n- **Enable borrowing** by tracking seat demand and allowing dynamic reallocation among priority levels\n\n### Boundaries\n\n**Upstream dependencies:**\n- APF Controller (`apf_controller.go`) provisions QueueSets per priority level, manages configurations\n- Flow Schema matching determines request classification and hash value for shuffle sharding\n- Request rate limiting filter (`apf_filter.go`) invokes StartRequest/Finish lifecycle\n\n**Downstream dependencies:**\n- Metrics system observes queue depths, waiting/executing request counts, seat concurrency, and epoch advances\n- EventClock interface provides real and virtual time for progress meter advancement\n- Promise mechanism (WriteOnce) coordinates dispatch decision communication between dispatch loop and request waiter\n\n**Not in scope:**\n- Flow Schema evaluation or request matching (upstream responsibility)\n- Exempt request handling (separate fast path, no queuing)\n- Per-request authentication or authorization validation\n\n### Key Architectural Constraints\n\n1. **Lock discipline:** All mutable queue state is protected by a single queueSet-level mutex. Virtual time updates (syncTimeLocked) must precede state mutations.\n2. **Promise-based dispatch:** Dispatch decisions are communicated via a WriteOnce promise set under lock; request threads wait without lock to avoid deadlock.\n3. **No cross-priority-level coordination:** Each QueueSet operates independently; borrowing is managed at the controller level by adjusting ConcurrencyLimits.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### QueueSet (`queueset.go`, `types.go`)\n\nThe core fair-queuing engine. Fields (under lock):\n\n| Field | Responsibility |\n|-------|---|\n| `queues []*queue` | Ordered array of fair-share queues, index tracked per request arrival |\n| `currentR SeatSeconds` | Global virtual time (progress meter), advanced by syncTimeLocked |\n| `dealer *Dealer` | Shuffle sharding parameters; picks a queue via entropy from request hash |\n| `totSeatsInUse`, `totSeatsWaiting` | Tracks seat occupancy for concurrency enforcement |\n| `totRequestsWaiting`, `totRequestsExecuting` | Metrics for queue depth and execution |\n\n**Key invariants:**\n- Virtual time only moves forward; epoch advancement prevents overflow (lines 489-522)\n- Every request in a queue has `arrivalR ≤ queue.nextDispatchR` (anti-windup bound, line 952-963)\n- Seats in use never exceed `dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit` except during grace periods for large single requests\n\n### Queue (`types.go`)\n\nRepresents a fair-share queue within a QueueSet. Fields:\n\n| Field | Responsibility |\n|-------|---|\n| `requestsWaiting fifo` | FIFO list of requests awaiting dispatch |\n| `requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]` | Requests currently executing from this queue |\n| `nextDispatchR SeatSeconds` | Virtual start time of the queue's allocated window |\n| `seatsInUse int` | Total seats held by executing requests from this queue |\n\n**Why per-queue tracking?** Allows virtual time calculation to reflect per-flow fairness.\n\n### Request (`types.go`)\n\nTracks a request's state through the system. Lifecycle:\n\n1. Created in `shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked` with `arrivalR = currentR`\n2. Enqueued into selected queue's `requestsWaiting` FIFO\n3. Dequeued in `dispatchLocked`, moved to queue's `requestsExecuting`, decision set to `decisionExecute`\n4. Request thread calls `Finish(execute)`, which calls `finishRequestLocked`\n5. Seats may linger if `AdditionalLatency > 0` (multi-phase request completion)\n\n**Work estimate tracking:**\n- `InitialSeats`: seats for primary execution phase\n- `FinalSeats` + `AdditionalLatency`: seats held post-completion (L7 processing, response marshaling)\n- Actual service duration adjusts queue's virtual start via `queue.nextDispatchR -= (G - S) * width`\n\n### FIFO List (`fifo_list.go`)\n\nA doubly-linked list with O(1) removal via closure. Tracks aggregate `queueSum` (InitialSeatsSum, MaxSeatsSum, TotalWorkSum) to avoid O(n) scans when selecting queues during shuffle sharding.\n\n### Shuffle Sharding Dealer (`shufflesharding.go`)\n\nImplements a card-dealing algorithm (entropy consumption: `log₂(deckSize) × handSize` bits). Given a hash value:\n\n1. Randomly select `handSize` queue indices from `deckSize` total queues\n2. Among selected hand, pick the queue with the **minimum total work** in waiting requests\n3. Reuse the same hand across multiple arrivals to reduce variance\n\n**Why shuffle sharding?** Prevents hash collisions from concentrating misbehaving flows into a single queue, improving isolation.\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Request Flow with Concrete Evidence\n\n### Phase 1: Request Arrival (StartRequest)\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:308-356`\n\n```\nStartRequest(ctx, workEstimate, hashValue, fsName, ...)\n  ↓ lockAndSyncTime(ctx)  // acquire lock; sync virtual time\n  ↓ syncTimeLocked(ctx)   // advance currentR based on elapsed real time\n     • incrR = (min(totSeatsInUse, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues) * timeSinceLast\n     • if currentR ≥ highR, call advanceEpoch to prevent overflow\n  ↓ Case 1: DesiredNumQueues < 1 (exempt fast path)\n     • canAccommodateSeatsLocked checks if max seat requirement ≤ available\n     • dispatchSansQueueLocked creates request, immediately sets decision=decisionExecute\n     • return (req, false)\n  ↓ Case 2: DesiredNumQueues ≥ 1 (queued path)\n     • shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked(workEstimate, hashValue, ...)\n       ├─ shuffleShardLocked: dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue)\n       │  ├─ random permutation via entropy bits\n       │  └─ pick queue with min(queueSum.TotalWorkSum)\n       ├─ rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked\n       │  ├─ reject if totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit AND curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit\n       │  └─ else enqueueToBoundLocked:\n       │     ├─ if queue was empty, set queue.nextDispatchR = currentR\n       │     ├─ enqueue to queue.requestsWaiting FIFO\n       │     ├─ update metrics (requests waiting, seats waiting, queue length)\n       │     └─ return request\n       └─ return req or nil (if rejected)\n  ↓ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked\n     • loop: while totRequestsWaiting > 0 AND totSeatsInUse < ConcurrencyLimit\n       ├─ findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked: round-robin through queues\n       │  ├─ scan for queue with min(queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork())\n       │  ├─ check canAccommodateSeatsLocked\n       │  └─ if cannot accommodate, set AdditionalLatency to preserve work\n       └─ dispatchLocked: dequeue from winning queue, set decision=decisionExecute\n  ↓ unlock\n  ↓ return (req, isIdleLocked)\n```\n\n**Key metric updates at arrival:** `RequestsWaiting.Add(1)`, `SeatsWaiting += maxSeats`, `SeatDemandIntegrator.Set(...)`\n\n### Phase 2: Request Dispatch\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:695-743`\n\nThe dispatch loop runs **synchronously** inside StartRequest. Virtual time must be consistent during dispatch because multiple requests may be dispatched in the same call.\n\n```\ndispatchLocked() → findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()\n  ↓ Round-robin through queues (starting after last dispatched queue)\n  ↓ For each non-empty queue:\n     • peekOldest from requestsWaiting\n     • compute currentVirtualFinish = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()\n     • track min(currentVirtualFinish)\n  ↓ Check if winning queue's head can accommodate seats\n     • if canAccommodateSeatsLocked fails:\n       ├─ wait for executing requests to complete\n       ├─ return (nil, nil) → no dispatch\n       └─ metrics.AddDispatchWithNoAccommodation\n  ↓ Handle multi-seated final phase\n     • if FinalSeats > ConcurrencyLimit:\n       ├─ reduce FinalSeats to ConcurrencyLimit\n       ├─ adjust AdditionalLatency to preserve total work\n  ↓ Set robinIndex for next round\n  ↓ Decision: set decision.Set(decisionExecute)\n     • if promise already resolved (request cancelled), don't move to executing\n  ↓ Move to queue.requestsExecuting\n  ↓ Advance queue's virtual start:\n     queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n  ↓ Return (queue, request)\n```\n\n**Anti-windup hack (boundNextDispatchLocked, line 952-963):**\nPrevent a low-demand queue from accumulating a negative virtual start:\n```go\nif queue.nextDispatchR < oldestWaiting.arrivalR {\n    queue.nextDispatchR = oldestWaiting.arrivalR\n}\n```\nThis ensures dispatch never precedes arrival in the virtual world.\n\n### Phase 3: Request Execution & Completion (Finish)\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:381-441` (request wrapper), `queueset.go:863-943` (finishRequestLocked)\n\n```\nreq.Finish(execFn)\n  ↓ req.wait()  // without lock\n     • decisionAny := req.decision.Get()  // blocks until dispatch decision made\n     • lockAndSyncTime(req.ctx)\n     • if decisionAny == decisionCancel (context expired before dispatch):\n       ├─ remove from queue\n       ├─ update metrics (requests rejected, timeout)\n       └─ return (false, isIdleLocked)\n     • else decisionExecute:\n       └─ return (true, false)\n  ↓ if execute:\n     • defer finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible(req)\n     • execFn()  // run user code\n  ↓ finishRequestLocked(req)\n     • actualServiceDuration := now - req.startTime\n     • adjust queue.nextDispatchR by (G - actualServiceDuration) * width\n     • update totSeatsInUse -= maxSeats\n     • if AdditionalLatency > 0:\n       ├─ schedule delayed seat release via EventAfterDuration\n       └─ metrics for lingering seats\n     • remove from queue.requestsExecuting\n     • try removeQueueIfEmptyLocked if queue exceeds desired count\n  ↓ dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()  // cascade dispatch\n  ↓ return isIdleLocked\n```\n\n**Why two-phase seat release?**\nInitialSeats are released when actual work completes. FinalSeats (e.g., response marshaling) are held for AdditionalLatency to avoid blocking the next request. This improves pipelining.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Virtual Time & Fairness Algorithm\n\n### Virtual Time Advancement (syncTimeLocked)\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:465-479`\n\n```\nsyncTimeLocked(ctx):\n  realNow := clock.Now()\n  timeSinceLast := realNow - lastRealTime\n  lastRealTime = realNow\n\n  ratio := getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()\n    // = min(seatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n    // where seatsRequested = sum over queues of (seatsInUse + queueSum.MaxSeatsSum)\n\n  incrR := SeatsTimesDuration(ratio, timeSinceLast)\n  currentR += incrR\n\n  if currentR ≥ highR:\n    advanceEpoch()  // subtract rDecrement from all R values to prevent overflow\n```\n\n**Intuition:** Virtual time advances at a rate proportional to:\n- How much concurrency is in use vs. available (fairness to other flows)\n- How many non-empty queues are competing (fair share per queue)\n\n### Virtual Finish Time Calculation\n\nWhen a request is dequeued at time T with work estimate W:\n```\nvirtualFinishTime = queue.nextDispatchR + W\n```\n\nThe dispatch loop picks the queue with the **minimum virtual finish time**, ensuring FIFO within each queue but round-robin fairness across queues.\n\n### Work Estimate Adjustment\n\nAt finish, if actual service time S < estimated G:\n```\nqueue.nextDispatchR -= (G - S) * width\n```\n\nThis **penalizes** queues that underutilized their allocated time, preventing them from gaining unfair advantage from optimistic estimates.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### Failure Mode: Overflow Prevention\n\n**Risk:** Virtual time counter can overflow (64-bit signed SeatSeconds).\n\n**Mitigation (advanceEpoch, line 489-522):**\n- When `currentR ≥ highR = rDecrement + rDecrement/2`, subtract `rDecrement = MaxSeatSeconds/2` from all R values\n- Applied to: `currentR`, all `queue.nextDispatchR`, all `request.arrivalR`\n- Logged as `AddEpochAdvance` metric\n\n**Tradeoff:** Periodic correction adds complexity but avoids unbounded R growth over months of operation.\n\n### Failure Mode: Concurrent Wide Requests\n\n**Risk:** A single request with `MaxSeats > ConcurrencyLimit` can fail to dispatch.\n\n**Mitigation (canAccommodateSeatsLocked, line 748-769):**\n```go\nif seats > qs.dCfg.ConcurrencyLimit:\n    if qs.totRequestsExecuting == 0:\n        return true  // Allow it to run alone\n    else:\n        return false  // Wait for others to finish\n```\nThis enforces **exclusive execution** for requests wider than the concurrency limit.\n\n**Tradeoff:** May block other requests unfairly, but prevents deadlock. Mitigated by work estimator bounds (typically max 15% of limit).\n\n### Failure Mode: Queue Starvation During Reconfiguration\n\n**Risk:** If `DesiredNumQueues` is reduced, empty queues are removed by attrition. A queue with stuck requests might linger.\n\n**Mitigation (removeQueueIfEmptyLocked, line 966-984):**\n- Only remove queue if:\n  - `len(queues) > DesiredNumQueues` AND\n  - `queue.requestsWaiting.Length() == 0` AND\n  - `queue.requestsExecuting.Len() == 0`\n- Update `robinIndex` if removed queue was at or before current position\n\n**Tradeoff:** Manual draining required; admins must monitor `queue.requestsWaiting.Length()` to ensure cleanup.\n\n### Design Tradeoff: Shuffle Sharding Parameters\n\n| Setting | Effect | Tradeoff |\n|---------|--------|----------|\n| `queues=1` | No shuffle sharding; all flows share one queue | Simple, fair allocation; misbehaving flow starves others |\n| `queues=128, handSize=4` | Each flow hashed to one of C(128,4) hands | Good isolation; higher entropy cost, memory overhead |\n| `handSize=handSize` near `queues` | More selective queue picking | Isolation but higher lock contention if many flows |\n\n**Guidance:** handSize typically 4–8; queues scaled to expected flow count.\n\n### Design Tradeoff: Estimated Service Duration (G)\n\n**Current:** Fixed at 3ms per QueueSet (line 215 in queueset.go).\n\n**Effect:**\n- Used to estimate initial work: `InitialWork = InitialSeats * G`\n- Used to penalize underutilization: `queue.nextDispatchR -= (G - actual) * width`\n\n**Tradeoff:**\n- Too high: Queues underutilize allocated time, starving other queues\n- Too low: Overestimate work, inflate queue's virtual finish time, allow preemption\n- Fixed value assumes uniform request characteristics; not tunable per priority level\n\n**Mitigation:** Request.AdditionalLatency allows explicit work accounting post-completion.\n\n### Design Tradeoff: Single Global Lock\n\nAll mutable queue state is protected by `queueSet.lock`.\n\n**Benefit:** Simple correctness reasoning; atomic state updates.\n\n**Cost:**\n- Lock contention under high request rate\n- StartRequest must synchronously dispatch requests (cannot pipeline)\n- Mitigation: `syncTimeLocked` deferred until next lock acquisition to reduce critical section\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### Promise Factory (testability)\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:47-54`\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactory func(initial, doneCtx, doneVal) promise.WriteOnce\ntype promiseFactoryFactory func(*queueSet) promiseFactory\n```\n\nDefault: `ordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory` returns `promise.NewWriteOnce`.\n\n**Extension:** Test code can provide a different factory to control promise resolution timing, simulate slow dispatch, or verify dispatch order.\n\n**Risk:** Incorrect factory can cause deadlocks or race conditions; not recommended for production use.\n\n### Clock Interface\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:86`, `fairqueuing/eventclock/interface.go`\n\nQueueSet uses an `eventclock.Interface` for:\n- `Now()`: current time for virtual time advancement\n- `EventAfterDuration(func, duration)`: schedule delayed seat release\n\n**Extension:** Custom clocks (e.g., simulation time) allow deterministic testing.\n\n**Risk:** Clock skew or backwards time can cause virtual time inversion or epoch advances to fail validation (line 507-509).\n\n### Metrics Integration\n\n**Code reference:** `metrics/metrics.go`\n\nQueueSet reports to:\n- `RatioedGaugePair.RequestsWaiting/Executing`: per-queue, per-flow-schema\n- `RatioedGauge.ExecSeatsGauge`: per-priority-level\n- `Gauge.SeatDemandIntegrator`: integral of (executing + waiting seats) over time\n\n**Extension:** Controller uses integrator output to drive borrowing adjustments (seat demand stats smoothing).\n\n**Risk:** Incorrect metrics can mask actual queue state; useful for observability but not for control decisions.\n\n### Dump for Debugging\n\n**Code reference:** `queueset.go:996-1015`\n\n```go\nfunc (qs *queueSet) Dump(includeRequestDetails bool) debug.QueueSetDump\n```\n\nReturns instant snapshot of all queues, requests, and metrics (including user info if requested). Used by debug endpoints.\n\n**Extension:** Can be called from outside lock to expose internal state without blocking.\n\n**Risk:** Snapshot inconsistency under high load; suitable only for offline debugging, not runtime decision-making.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications & Failure Scenarios\n\n### Performance Implications\n\n#### Lock Contention\n\nUnder high request rates (e.g., 10k req/sec per QueueSet):\n- Each StartRequest acquires lock, syncs time, dispatches requests\n- Expected hold time: 100–500 μs per lock (dispatch loop iterations + FIFO ops)\n- If CPU-bound: lock contention can spike tail latencies\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Increase `DesiredNumQueues` to reduce per-queue depth (shallower FIFO searches)\n- Distribute flows across multiple priority levels if possible\n- Monitor `apiserver_flowcontrol_*_lock_*` metrics (if available)\n\n#### Virtual Time Skew Under Bursty Load\n\nIf execution is bursty (e.g., GC pause), virtual time may lag:\n```\nincrR = min(actualSeats, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues * timeSinceLast\n```\nDuring pause, `actualSeats` drops, so `incrR` ≈ 0. When requests resume, accumulated waiting requests have `arrivalR << currentR`, causing them to dispatch FIFO (fairness breaks temporarily).\n\n**Mitigation:** Virtual time is local to each priority level; system GC less likely to affect all levels equally.\n\n#### Epoch Advance Overhead\n\n`advanceEpoch` walks all queues and all waiting requests (O(Q + W) where Q = queue count, W = waiting requests). Under heavy queueing (100k+ waiting requests), this can stall dispatch for milliseconds.\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- Tune `estimatedServiceDuration` to reduce work estimates (less queue depth)\n- Monitor `AddEpochAdvance` metric; if frequent, investigate cause (e.g., concurrency limit too low)\n\n### Reliability Implications\n\n#### Queue Draining on Priority Level Reconfiguration\n\nWhen a priority level is reconfigured (e.g., `DesiredNumQueues` decreased):\n1. New requests hash to remaining queues\n2. Old queues drain by attrition (removeQueueIfEmptyLocked)\n3. Until queue is empty, robinIndex remains valid\n\n**Risk:** Stuck requests prevent queue removal. Admins must monitor queue depth and manually investigate if queue doesn't drain within expected time.\n\n**Mitigation:** Set up alerts on `apiserver_flowcontrol_queues_length_*` metric; investigate requests with long `ArriveTime - StartTime`.\n\n#### Metrics Staleness During High Concurrency\n\n`SeatDemandIntegrator` tracks integral of seat usage. Under extreme concurrency:\n- Integrator value is only updated when:\n  - Request enqueued\n  - Request dequeued\n  - Request finishes\n- If no changes occur, integrator value lags real demand\n\n**Mitigation:** Integrator is smoothed (half-life ~5 min) before borrowing decisions; short-term fluctuations don't affect concurrency allocation.\n\n### Observability & Debugging\n\n**Key metrics to monitor:**\n\n| Metric | Interpretation |\n|--------|---|\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_queues_length_*` | Queue depth per priority level; increasing → admission too high or dispatch slow |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_seat_demand_*` | Integral of occupied seats; used for borrowing decisions |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_epoch_advance_total` | How often virtual time is reset; high frequency → R values large, possible performance impact |\n| `apiserver_flowcontrol_dispatch_with_no_accommodation` | Requests waiting for seats to free up; high → concurrency limit too low or request widths too high |\n\n**Debug endpoint** (`/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_queues`):\n- Provides per-queue snapshot with request details\n- Useful to correlate metrics with actual queue state\n- Can be called frequently without lock contention (outside queueset lock)\n\n---\n\n## 8. Important Files and Directory Map\n\n### Core QueueSet Implementation\n\n| Path | Responsibility |\n|------|---|\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/interface.go` | QueueSet, Request, QueueSetFactory interfaces; QueuingConfig, DispatchingConfig |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/queueset.go` | queueSet struct, StartRequest, dispatch loop, virtual time sync, epoch advance |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/types.go` | request, queue, queueSum structs; work estimation helpers |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/fifo_list.go` | FIFO list with O(1) removal; queue sum tracking |\n| `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/queueset/doc.go` | Fair queuing algorithm explanation; Summary Table: Request Lifecycle State Transitions\n\n| State | Condition | Location | Next |\n|-------|-----------|----------|------|\n| Created | In `StartRequest`, hash computed | queueset.go:560 | → Rejected or Queued |\n| Rejected | `rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked` returns false | queueset.go:574 | END (return nil) |\n| Queued | Enqueued in `queue.requestsWaiting` | queueset.go:643 | → Dispatched or Cancelled |\n| Dispatched | `dispatchLocked` moves to `queue.requestsExecuting`, decision=decisionExecute | queueset.go:710–727 | → Executing |\n| Executing | Request handler runs `execFn` | queueset.go:391 | → Finished |\n| Cancelled | Context cancelled before dispatch, decision=decisionCancel | queueset.go:415 | END (return false) |\n| Finished | `finishRequestLocked` called, seats released or scheduled for release | queueset.go:863–943 | END (return idle) |\n\n---\n\n## 10. Conclusion\n\nThe APF QueueSet is a sophisticated fair-queuing implementation that balances **fairness** (virtual time), **isolation** (shuffle sharding), **concurrency control** (seat-based limiting), and **adaptability** (borrowing). Its success depends on:\n\n1. **Accurate work estimates** to tune virtual time advancement\n2. **Appropriate queue counts** to reduce per-queue depth and lock contention\n3. **Careful priority level configuration** to align with actual request patterns\n4. **Monitoring key metrics** (queue depth, seat demand, epoch advances) to detect imbalances\n\nOperational risks are primarily around **queue draining during reconfiguration**, **lock contention under extreme load**, and **overflow protection** via periodic epoch advances. Understanding these tradeoffs is essential for effective APF tuning and troubleshooting in production Kubernetes clusters.\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
